  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26651e8f-73b6-4c2d-aa68-9dee19f2939b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8677952510187638168">The startling, universally acclaimed breakthrough YA novel from master bestselling author Alice Hoffman, now in paperback.<br/><br/>Left on her own when her family dies in a terrible disaster, fifteen-year-old Green is haunted by loss and by the past.   <span id="freeText8677952510187638168" style="display:none">The startling, universally acclaimed breakthrough YA novel from master bestselling author Alice Hoffman, now in paperback.<br /><br />Left on her own when her family dies in a terrible disaster, fifteen-year-old Green is haunted by loss and by the past. Struggling to survive physically and emotionally in a place where nothing seems to grow and ashes are everywhere, Green retreats into the ruined realm of her garden. But in destroying her feelings, she also begins to destroy herself, erasing the girl she'd once been as she inks darkness into her skin. It is only through a series of mysterious encounters that Green can relearn the lessons of love and begin to heal enough to tell her story.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I have read both books, I did not even realize there was a second one at first because the first one, I agree, didn't seem to need a sequel. However I<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I have read both books, I did not even realize there was a second one at first because the first one, I agree, didn't seem to need a sequel. However I really did love the second one just as much as the first one. Though I do think that you need to be in the right place in your life to really get into the books, to some extent they do remind me of poetry. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_192108453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192108453" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192108453?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192108453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17057748236262302265">Alice Hoffman by way of Cormac McCarthy. Fifteen-year-old, raven-haired, and green-thumbed Green would love to go to the market with her parents and her practically moon-glowing sister, but someone needs to stay behind and take care of things. The three most important things after location, location, location are timing, timing, and timing. The family picked the wrong day to bring produce to the city. A fire. Think London, 1666, with a dash of 9/11. Green not only loses her family but is affecte</span>
  <span id="freeText17057748236262302265" style="display:none">Alice Hoffman by way of Cormac McCarthy. Fifteen-year-old, raven-haired, and green-thumbed Green would love to go to the market with her parents and her practically moon-glowing sister, but someone needs to stay behind and take care of things. The three most important things after location, location, location are timing, timing, and timing. The family picked the wrong day to bring produce to the city. A fire. Think London, 1666, with a dash of 9/11. Green not only loses her family but is affected physically as well, as ash from the event damages her eyes, reducing her vision severely, but not entirely. Cormac-like events beset poor Green. Nothing will grow in her precious garden. She survives, inking her skin with dark images reflective of the new reality, writing over who she was with who she needs to be to survive. <br /><br />Hoffman uses the hellscape, a very Road-evocative environment as the foil, the struggle Green must take on. How Green grows, changes, redefines herself as someone outside her parents, her family, and redefines herself again to cope with changing circumstances, how she finds ways to survive, how she copes with other survivors, human and animal, and struggles with connection and loss makes for a compelling and moving story. <br /><br />This being Alice Hoffman there is a fairy tale feel to the tale. Grimm indeed. She tosses in some bits of magical realism, or maybe just plain magic, and a lot of feeling. <br /><br />This is a YA title and is a very fast read, 116 small pages, and I so wish it had been much longer, as it is satisfying beyond its length, even for a geezer like me.<br /><br /><b>Other Hoffman books I have reviewed</b>:<br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36731906" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Local Girls</a><br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198297394" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Blackbird House</a><br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36729919" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ice Queen</a><br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148554768" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Red Garden</a><br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1229696636" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dovekeepers</a><br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172258848" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rules of Magic</a><br />-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3026588529" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The World That We Knew</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17057748236262302265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18198569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18198569" />
    <a title="Tawny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1001935-tawny"><img alt="Tawny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262748718p2/1001935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18198569?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tawny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tawny" href="/user/show/1001935-tawny">Tawny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18198569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8878720637332052530">Author: Alice Hoffman<br/>Title: Green Angel<br/>Genre: magical realism, tale of survival<br/>Publication Info: Scholastic. New York. 2003.<br/>Recommended Age: 13 and older<br/><br/>Plot Summary: Green, a moody, introspective 15-year-old, stays at home while her parents and younger sister travel to the city to sell their vegetable produce. Being intentionally left behind to tend the garden causes her to not say goodbye to her family. From across the river, Green watches in horror as the city explodes into flames. Even at he</span>
  <span id="freeText8878720637332052530" style="display:none">Author: Alice Hoffman<br />Title: Green Angel<br />Genre: magical realism, tale of survival<br />Publication Info: Scholastic. New York. 2003.<br />Recommended Age: 13 and older<br /><br />Plot Summary: Green, a moody, introspective 15-year-old, stays at home while her parents and younger sister travel to the city to sell their vegetable produce. Being intentionally left behind to tend the garden causes her to not say goodbye to her family. From across the river, Green watches in horror as the city explodes into flames. Even at her distance, she is not kept safe from embers entering her eyes. She becomes partially blinded. She waits for her family for days, but they never return. Green feels guilty for her previous behavior. She punishes herself by carving dark tattoos all over her body. The outside world is in anarchy and even Green—having a supernatural talent for gardening—refuses to help the suffering plants from the ash that blankets them. By putting on a tough front, she protects herself from looters and others who try to cheat her. She even sews thorns and pounds nails into her clothing so that no one can get close to her. Several surviving animals and people come into Green’s life and somehow restore her love of nature and life. One boy shows up long enough to help replant the garden and instill in Green a reason for living again. At the end of the book, her vision is restored and she sets out to tell her story of heartache and survival.<br /><br />Personal Notes: I found the book hard to grasp at times. This may have been because of the magical realism. There were times the story seemed hauntingly real, and other times where things just did not make sense. For example, why were so many youth who had lost their families allowed to live on the streets and on their own? Where was the police? Child Protective Services? Extended family members? I had a hard time imagining her needing to sell off all the family belongings for food and making bread out of ground chestnuts for so long. I wouldn’t really know how to go about teaching this book in the classroom, so I would recommend it for individual reading only. <br /><br />Evaluation: This book is somewhat difficult to read. It delves into some deep issues of survival, solitude, and hope. While written for a younger audience, the story also calls for sophisticated readers. I think that students with a taste for the gothic would particularly enjoy this story.<br /><br />Other Comments: I wonder if this book was written with the intent to help youth cope with the horrors of 9/11. The actual disaster in the story was not explained well at all. It was quite confusing, really. What would cause the whole city to shake and burn down? Why would people have felt the need to jump from the buildings? These are some of the questions I had while reading the novel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8878720637332052530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_284921745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284921745" />
    <a title="Linda Lipko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1544522-linda-lipko"><img alt="Linda Lipko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354220736p2/1544522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284921745?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Lipko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Lipko" href="/user/show/1544522-linda-lipko">Linda Lipko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284921745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9612578023813853015">When reading another Alice Hoffman book, I'm reminded that she is one of my favorite authors. She consistently weaves magic into characters that have a mystical, yet down to earth, quality about them.<br/><br/>The setting of this haunting book is a town and countryside destroyed by a terrible conflagration.<br/><br/>Using metaphorical symbolism, Hoffman tells the tale of Green who stayed behind on the day her mother, father and sister went to town to sell their vegetables. Resentful, Green does not say goodbye. Thu</span>
  <span id="freeText9612578023813853015" style="display:none">When reading another Alice Hoffman book, I'm reminded that she is one of my favorite authors. She consistently weaves magic into characters that have a mystical, yet down to earth, quality about them.<br /><br />The setting of this haunting book is a town and countryside destroyed by a terrible conflagration.<br /><br />Using metaphorical symbolism, Hoffman tells the tale of Green who stayed behind on the day her mother, father and sister went to town to sell their vegetables. Resentful, Green does not say goodbye. Thus, when her family perishes in the fire, she bears tremendous guilt.<br /><br />As the sky is gray, blocking the sun, the land is unproductive and societal rules seem to fall apart. What remains is a band of people who eek out a living, some of whom cannot overcome their grief and live sad apathetic lives.<br /><br />Green remains cut off and lives alone, hardened and thorny. As slowly she reaches out to a neighbor, a dog, a few birds and a forsaken emotionally distraught young woman, Ash begins the process of healing.<br /><br />In her usual style, Hoffman transforms the character in a fairytale fashion. Thorns and nettles are replaced with new growth of food as the ash is pushed aside to allow earth that produces and inner strength that rejuvenates.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9612578023813853015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4952665080731207944">This story was beautifully written. Each and every phrase evocative of a deeper meaning, that i honestly find myself lacking the proper words to describe how much i liked it. Liked it, is just too insignicant... i guess it becamed part of me, as only the greatest stories; the ones that truly touch our hearts, are capable of doing it.   <span id="freeText4952665080731207944" style="display:none">This story was beautifully written. Each and every phrase evocative of a deeper meaning, that i honestly find myself lacking the proper words to describe how much i liked it. Liked it, is just too insignicant... i guess it becamed part of me, as only the greatest stories; the ones that truly touch our hearts, are capable of doing it. If we let them...<br /><br />For me, this author is outstanding in this gender. She weaves the most sad, heartbreaking stories, in perfect tapestries, made of memories and ghosts, tears and love.<br /><br />This is the story of fifteen year old Green. The older daughter, the quiet daughter...<br /><br /><i>I was the least among them, nothing special, just a girl. I was a moody, dark weed; still, they<br />called me Green because of my talents in the garden</i><br /><br />When her sister and parents are killed, Green's starts to disappear beneath the cover of <b>thorns</b><br /><br /> <i>One night when the sky was ash-coloured, I went into the ruined garden and clipped the thorns from the bare rosebushes, then sewed them to my clothes, one by one, until my fingers bled. Now I was ready to feel nothing. I was protected from feeling anything at all.</i><br /><br />and <b>tattoos</b>....<br /><br /><i>I didn't deserve anything, not food to ease my hunger or water to<br />ease my thirst.(..) That was when I took a pin and some black ink. I began to mark my arm. I outlined a raven, and then a bat, then a rose that looked like a flower found at the end of the world. That's who I was now without my mother and my father and my moonlit sister. Blood and ink.<br />Darkness where before there had been patience, black where there'd once been green.</i><br /><br />...that she starts using as <b>armor</b> against the world, even against herself.<br /><br /> After a while, Green starts to give place to Ash. A girl that lives among ashes and pain...a girl whose own sight becomes cloudy...<br /><br />This is a story about surviving grief.<br /><br />A evocative, quirky, sad little story, sprinkled with bits of wisdom as just Alice Hoffman is capable of doing. I'm looking forward to read the next one <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6636138.Green_Witch__Green_Angel___2_" title="Green Witch (Green Angel, #2) by Alice Hoffman" rel="nofollow noopener">Green Witch</a>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12908274649995869939">This lyrical and lushly descriptive novella captures a young woman’s grieving process with razor-sharp precision. When Green’s family leave for the city one day, she has no way of knowing that she will never see them again, as a terrible disaster destroys much of the city and surrounding country. Green retreats into herself, building walls both mental and physical, tattooing herself with black roses and ravens in an attempt to transform herself into Ash, a girl who cannot be hurt by loss:<br/><br/><i>”I was </i></span>
  <span id="freeText12908274649995869939" style="display:none">This lyrical and lushly descriptive novella captures a young woman’s grieving process with razor-sharp precision. When Green’s family leave for the city one day, she has no way of knowing that she will never see them again, as a terrible disaster destroys much of the city and surrounding country. Green retreats into herself, building walls both mental and physical, tattooing herself with black roses and ravens in an attempt to transform herself into Ash, a girl who cannot be hurt by loss:<br /><br /><i>”I was making a different sort of heart, one that was black, one that was protected by thorns, by bats, by raven’s wings, by sorrow, by my aloneness, my armor</i>.” The gradual healing of the blasted landscape around her mirrors the process by which Green learns to feel and love again, rediscovering herself.<br /><br />After my indifference to her two earlier children's books, <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/195672.Aquamarine__Water_Tales___1_" title="Aquamarine (Water Tales, #1) by Alice Hoffman" rel="nofollow noopener">Aquamarine</a>
</u> and <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/333115.Indigo__Water_Tales___2_" title="Indigo (Water Tales, #2) by Alice Hoffman" rel="nofollow noopener">Indigo</a>
</u>, I almost gave Hoffman's <u>Green Angel</u> a miss, which would have been a shame. She seems finally to have hit her stride in this third novel for younger readers, which I found beautifully written, and quite moving.</span>

<div id="review_195671088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195671088" />
    <a title="N.T. Embe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5395467-n-t-embe"><img alt="N.T. Embe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537744425p2/5395467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195671088?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="N.T. Embe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="N.T. Embe" href="/user/show/5395467-n-t-embe">N.T. Embe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439443845" href="/book/show/899200.Green_Angel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">For those of you lost and deep in the darkness of the world, this is for you.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to N.T. by: </span>
      Library
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195671088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4983113841864271249">A story like this will never grow old. It is timeless as the sun, the moon, and the stars in the sky. As ageless as the trees and the grasses in all their richness in summer, and all their love in fall. It is the story of rebirth and, most of all, of Hope... and how that hope will grow from the darkest depths of anyone's prisons. Horrors, pain unimaginable, loneliness, sorrow unending--all these ashes that cover our souls, and darken our days.... This is the story we live through. Through the so</span>
  <span id="freeText4983113841864271249" style="display:none">A story like this will never grow old. It is timeless as the sun, the moon, and the stars in the sky. As ageless as the trees and the grasses in all their richness in summer, and all their love in fall. It is the story of rebirth and, most of all, of Hope... and how that hope will grow from the darkest depths of anyone's prisons. Horrors, pain unimaginable, loneliness, sorrow unending--all these ashes that cover our souls, and darken our days.... This is the story we live through. Through the softest, gentlest, most profound of ways, this is the story we read in <i>Green Angel</i>, and it is the story we are born again through.<br /><br />I do not know where to even begin to describe the profound impact this story had on me. It has settled in my heart like the heaviest of stones, but one that I know is not only a mere stone. It is a seed. A seed, or perhaps an egg--there settled in my chest, awaiting the chance to softly break, to steadily expand, to spread itself from the depths of me, throughout every muscle, every strand of nerve and thought--to become actions, to be born of dreams and turn into reality. It is like a magic spell, that captures the mind's attention so surely that you are swept away in this river, and are not aware you've been swallowed whole until in a sudden blink, you awaken to find yourself drenched and heavy with the tale. It brings a hand over one's heart, or a bittersweet tear and smile to our faces; it echoes like sorrow so close, and like laughter in the midst of pain. It is a book of memories. A creation so deeply endowed with emotions and the murmurings of the heart that our own hearts wrench in its presence, are torn from within us, beg to be close--because they know those feelings; they have each been there. We are all a witness to that pain. We have all ached and lost so deeply. We can all walk in the ashes. Sometimes, we still remember or know what it is to be lost in them--nothing but ash yourself.<br /><br />*Smiles gently* ...and then... throughout the midst of our sorrows, our loss... in this shadowed world we have come walking into... like pale beauty, a sun we cannot see, a moon we long greeted only with cries, the stars we shed tears to--softly the warmth of color shades this world. A faint spot: in the earth, on the shelf, or suddenly looking up and noticing: the sky is <i>blue</i>~ ...how blessed that first recognition is of what we forgot: that this is, and forever will be--ours and ours undeniably!--<i>life.</i> ...how <i>great!</i> How the depth rushes around us, and suddenly we realize like the very earth and its offspring, the saplings that push up from the pallid dirt, that we are moving again--moving forward--and that we cannot stop ourselves. Our hearts, our souls--they will not let us.<br /><br />...this is the story of life again. Of going through the darkness, and finding the light. Of learning that to live is not impossible, even when silence and loneliness and the veil of apathy have claimed us. It is written elusively, and yet persuades the heart to listen and respond. All we have to do... is give it the chance to speak, and it will unfold worlds for us. Without words, without complications of language, or situation, or happenstance. Like fairy tales and magic, it will give us a meaning deeper than what words can weave. It takes only a willing heart--an open mind--to understand it.<br /><br />Though my review is cryptic for some, and too elusive for others, the book is one that speaks and is written from the heart. You have only to read the first few pages to realize why I have written in a manner so unfitting the everyday language of honest critique. *Smiles* I feel that this book deserved an emotive response, because for me, it is my memories, my present, my heart, and my soul it touched.<br /><br />Readers, give this book a shot. It is beauty without the need to describe itself as such. And it is a miracle of life that no one should turn away, even if you end up not enjoying some aspects of it. Look beyond that. Give it a chance. It can be liberating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4983113841864271249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_173595365" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173595365" />
    <a title="Wall-to-wall books - wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2281076-wall-to-wall-books---wendy"><img alt="Wall-to-wall books - wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1259761247p2/2281076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173595365?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wall-to-wall books - wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wall-to-wall books - wendy" href="/user/show/2281076-wall-to-wall-books---wendy">Wall-to-wall books - wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2281076-wall-to-wall-books---wendy?shelf=shelfari-favorites">shelfari-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173595365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9290019364836050143">Well this is nothing short of a truly AMAZING book! I absolutely loved it and can't wait to read "Green Witch" the sequel.<br/><br/>This book got real mixed reviews. In my opinion, the people who gave it a low rating just didn't "get it". There are books that are read purely for entertainment and those that have a deeper meaning. This is one of those books. Every single paragraph in this book is dripping with meaning. You don't have to read between the lines, you read into the lines. This book is "Magical</span>
  <span id="freeText9290019364836050143" style="display:none">Well this is nothing short of a truly AMAZING book! I absolutely loved it and can't wait to read "Green Witch" the sequel.<br /><br />This book got real mixed reviews. In my opinion, the people who gave it a low rating just didn't "get it". There are books that are read purely for entertainment and those that have a deeper meaning. This is one of those books. Every single paragraph in this book is dripping with meaning. You don't have to read between the lines, you read into the lines. This book is "Magical Realism" it is not meant to be real! So you have to read it with an open mind, knowing that this would not happen in real life, or would it?<br /><br />There are so many lines in this book that just grabbed me. One of them being - "I wanted silence, peace, blue skies, yesterday." When we are struck by tragedy, a death in the family, a fire, even a break-up, what do we wish for most? For it to have never have happened. We wish to go back in time. We wish for... yesterday.<br /><br />At the end of the book She says - "Every page white like a garden, in which anything might grow." again, what a beautiful line. Writing words on paper, forming a story is a lot like planting seeds in a garden. Words are seeds for our mind and how they grow is up to you, how you nurture, cultivate and harvest them.A garden is what you make of it, and a story is how you feel it, how you interpret it, and what you take away.<br /><br />This book is all about giving and receiving. Its more than just pay back, or paying a debt. It is just simply returning the favor, taking care of others that took care of you, maybe even a little of "Do unto others..." Heather hushed the others and told them to leave Green alone, in return Green left food and clothes for her. Green saved a couple baby birds, they in turn knitted a fishing net of her own hair. She nursed a dogs burned feet back to health, he in return shook the trees till all the chestnuts fell for her to gather. He also led her to her neighbor's house so she could find out it was the neighbor who threw the stones saving her from the looters. In return Green took her food. Green took in a boy who lost his mother, she shared her home and all her food with him. In return he cooked and re-started the burned garden.<br /><br />This book is about Re-birth and renewal. After a forest fire the forest renews itself. New shoots of green plants start growing. After a loved one dies, after all the sadness, you go through a re-birth, acceptance and living your life again. A town goes through a re-birth after a disaster (tornado, flood etc.) when they start rebuilding. This happens in so many ways in the book. Even Green herself goes through a huge re-birth, not only her appearance, her name, the house and garden, but also her spirit! Her soul and her heard is renewed.<br /><br />There is so much more to this book than just an amusing story. Allow yourself to dig deeper, allow yourself to feel, allow yourself into Green's world, only then will you truly "Get it". </span>
  <a data-text-id="9290019364836050143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11641876087492587713">Nothing spectacular--it's almost like a trial size sample of Alice Hoffman's writing. There's the usual fairytale like quality and hints of magical realism; standard Hoffman stuff. What's strange is the approach it takes. There's been some type of disaster (perhaps the result of some form of terrorism in this unnamed seeting), but we never get the back story as to what happened or why. Instead, the novella focuses on how the loss of her family and way of life affect the main character, Green. It</span>
  <span id="freeText11641876087492587713" style="display:none">Nothing spectacular--it's almost like a trial size sample of Alice Hoffman's writing. There's the usual fairytale like quality and hints of magical realism; standard Hoffman stuff. What's strange is the approach it takes. There's been some type of disaster (perhaps the result of some form of terrorism in this unnamed seeting), but we never get the back story as to what happened or why. Instead, the novella focuses on how the loss of her family and way of life affect the main character, Green. It's a quick and easy read, but not as gripping as perhaps a more fleshed out story would have been.</span>

<div id="review_157816947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157816947" />
    <a title="Ana Mardoll" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3078990-ana-mardoll"><img alt="Ana Mardoll" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519954099p2/3078990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157816947?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana Mardoll" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana Mardoll" href="/user/show/3078990-ana-mardoll">Ana Mardoll</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780545231244" href="/book/show/7663826-green-angel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3078990-ana-mardoll?shelf=ana-reviewed">ana-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157816947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16007371531893682255">Green Angel / 0-439-65878-0<br/><br/>This story of a young girl's loss of her entire family and her own identity, and the subsequent struggle to regain herself in the aftermath of the loss, will no doubt make an impression on anyone. The deep themes of loss and survivor guilt are explored thoroughly, against a backdrop of magical realism. <br/><br/>Somehow, "Green Angel" puts me in mind of "Island of the Blue Dolphins", for the titular character "Green" often seems just as isolated and alone, despite her interactio</span>
  <span id="freeText16007371531893682255" style="display:none">Green Angel / 0-439-65878-0<br /><br />This story of a young girl's loss of her entire family and her own identity, and the subsequent struggle to regain herself in the aftermath of the loss, will no doubt make an impression on anyone. The deep themes of loss and survivor guilt are explored thoroughly, against a backdrop of magical realism. <br /><br />Somehow, "Green Angel" puts me in mind of "Island of the Blue Dolphins", for the titular character "Green" often seems just as isolated and alone, despite her interactions with her neighbors and village people, largely due to the almost complete lack of dialogue throughout the book. And, like "Island of the Blue Dolphins", Green's survival and grasp on humanity is aided by numerous animals, each of which she gently nurses to health, cherishes, and finally frees, recognizing that being wild is an intrinsic part of *their* characters. <br /><br />Despite its deep themes and achingly lovely narrative, "Green Angel" will not please all audiences. The novel is extremely short - a little more than 100 pages - and the frequent repetition will enable quick readers to whip through in an hour or so. The novel relies heavily on magical realism, with Green often surviving on little more than a few nuts a day, and with health issues largely determined by the demands of the plot. Characters and themes drift in and out of the story, creating an aching, detached narrative to match Green's dissociation from her pain, but in such a way that may frustrate more literal-minded readers. <br /><br />"Green Angel" is worth trying, if only for the beauty of the prose and the painful themes contained within, and with such a short time investment to the novel, any reader owes it to themselves to check it out, and approach the novel with an open heart. And if you do read and enjoy "Green Angel", make certain to also read the even better sequel, "Green Witch".<br /><br />~ Ana Mardoll</span>
  <a data-text-id="16007371531893682255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90696132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90696132" />
    <a title="Blake Fraina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/860622-blake-fraina"><img alt="Blake Fraina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594167244p2/860622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90696132?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blake Fraina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blake Fraina" href="/user/show/860622-blake-fraina">Blake Fraina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90696132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17689311735312761146">Nearly forty years after Hiroshima/Nagasaki, two years after the WTC attacks and two years before the Hurricane Katrina disaster, Alice Hoffman published this spare, elegant and evergreen fable about apocalyptic catastrophe, loss, grief and, ultimately, healing. <br/><br/>It recalls two of my favourite childhood reads, Shirley Rousseau Murphy's [long out of print] <i>The Sand Ponies</i> and Patricia McKillip's seminal fantasy, <i>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</i>.<br/><br/>After losing her entire family in an unspecified (seemingl</span>
  <span id="freeText17689311735312761146" style="display:none">Nearly forty years after Hiroshima/Nagasaki, two years after the WTC attacks and two years before the Hurricane Katrina disaster, Alice Hoffman published this spare, elegant and evergreen fable about apocalyptic catastrophe, loss, grief and, ultimately, healing. <br /><br />It recalls two of my favourite childhood reads, Shirley Rousseau Murphy's [long out of print] <i>The Sand Ponies</i> and Patricia McKillip's seminal fantasy, <i>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</i>.<br /><br />After losing her entire family in an unspecified (seemingly nuclear) disaster, fifteen year old Green must fend for herself in a barren and desperate world. Nearly blind, starving and paralysed with grief, she slowly heals herself by reaching out to others (including a wounded greyhound, two orphaned birds, an injured hawk and a elderly neighbor) needier than herself while clinging to fond memories of the loving relationships with her parents and beloved twin sister, Aurora. <br /><br />Hoffman's skill as a novelist is apparent. Her prose is simple and dreamy, designed for maximum emotional impact. I wept several times in the story. I think that says a lot for a YA novel. This book offers a heartbreaking lesson in the importance of loving and letting go, as well as the necessity to rejoice in every moment of life. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17689311735312761146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_286968078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286968078" />
    <a title="Laurie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1050800-laurie"><img alt="Laurie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314166385p2/1050800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286968078?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie" href="/user/show/1050800-laurie">Laurie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286968078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6971694086088562889">Despite being a very long time fan of Hoffman’s, this is the first of her young adult work I’ve read. It’s a slim book, more of a fable or fairy tale than a conventional novel. Despite its brevity, it evokes strong feelings. <br/><br/>Green is 15 years old and gets left to tend the farm one day while her parents and sister head into the city to sell their produce at the market. Upset at missing out on the trip, she does not say goodbye to them; no worries, things will be worked out when they get home. But</span>
  <span id="freeText6971694086088562889" style="display:none">Despite being a very long time fan of Hoffman’s, this is the first of her young adult work I’ve read. It’s a slim book, more of a fable or fairy tale than a conventional novel. Despite its brevity, it evokes strong feelings. <br /><br />Green is 15 years old and gets left to tend the farm one day while her parents and sister head into the city to sell their produce at the market. Upset at missing out on the trip, she does not say goodbye to them; no worries, things will be worked out when they get home. But tragedy strikes; the city is destroyed that day and the huge fire even destroys much of the farm across the river. Her family is not coming home. Her home is covered with ashes, the garden gone, the leaves and fruit have fallen from the trees. Green, now taking the name of Ash, is stricken with grief and survivor guilt. This is her journey through grief; those who help her, her set backs, her slow recovery. It’s a beautiful little book, and a powerful one, written in a way that even a young child can understand and an adult will be enchanted by. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6971694086088562889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36974342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36974342" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1535156-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1236357238p2/1535156.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/1535156-shannon">Shannon</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1535156-shannon?shelf=good-fantasy-romance">good-fantasy-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36974342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7760446006162864042"><br/>Your book review is due Sunday, November 2 at midnight, and should include the following components:<br/>1. A 5-7 sentence summary (beginning, middle & end) of the book, including an explanation of the motive of the main character and the conflicts encountered.<br/>2. Your favorite line from the book and a 2-3 sentence explanation of what the line infers about the story, message OR main character.<br/>3. Review of book: 3-4 sentences about your opinion of the book, backed up with details, AND a justification o</span>
  <span id="freeText7760446006162864042" style="display:none"><br />Your book review is due Sunday, November 2 at midnight, and should include the following components:<br />1. A 5-7 sentence summary (beginning, middle &amp; end) of the book, including an explanation of the motive of the main character and the conflicts encountered.<br />2. Your favorite line from the book and a 2-3 sentence explanation of what the line infers about the story, message OR main character.<br />3. Review of book: 3-4 sentences about your opinion of the book, backed up with details, AND a justification of why you gave the number of stars you gave<br /><br />Green Angel by Alice Hoffman is the story of a girl named green who lives with her father mother and sister. One day her family goes into town intending to sell goods to the towns people,but a fire engulfs the city and the ashes waft to her home, getting in her eyes and making her partially blind. Green's parents and sister die in the fire. Green goes through a change in character. She changes her name to Ash and inks black roses, crows, and vines all over her body. Through the story she struggles with the traumatic experience and the imposing depression that fallows the death of her family. Through a chain of events she learns to be green again and is able to tell her families story and get on with her life.<br /><br />"Whenever I dreamed and my sister was beside me, I could breathe easier. Aurora's skin was silver, aglow with light. Sometimes in my dreams she had grown up and was my age exactly. Even as my twin she was still my beloved opposite: the moon, not brackish green water. Bright, not dim. Wild, not plodding and shy. She was my sister and she knew my thoughts before they were spoken. She knew why I couldn't bear to see. Why I wanted the cinders in my eyes. Why I never bothered going to my mother's medicine cabinet, where there were so many ointments and cures. My vision was little more than shadows, but even in my dreams, I wouldn't search for a cure." This excerpt truly conveys the amount of pain that Green is going through. It describes her grief her agony, her loneliness. It shows how terrible her loss is and how she wants nothing more than to fade into the background, fade away like her family. <br /><br />In my opinion the book Green Angel is one of my favorite books of all time. I would give it a four star rating. Green's story is so heartfelt, so very moving. Alice Hoffman shows the reader a side of grief that many are too afraid to speak of. She conveys the deep agony that goes with the loss of a loved one, she shows us that even though life may seem absolutely hopeless, even though there is nothing to live for; life has a way of giving us what we need, in the disparate times that we need them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7760446006162864042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164240436" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17924473777745387086">I read this book when I was a young child and fell in love with it. <br/><br/>May 17, 2014 - I bought this book when I began to remember the books I adored as a child. I am studying to become an elementary teacher so I can give the help and friendship I never got. I want to be the person I always needed in my life. I want to share with the children I teach the books that got me through my childhood and continue to get me through my young adult life. <br/><br/>This book is one of those that I remember from my childh</span>
  <span id="freeText17924473777745387086" style="display:none">I read this book when I was a young child and fell in love with it. <br /><br />May 17, 2014 - I bought this book when I began to remember the books I adored as a child. I am studying to become an elementary teacher so I can give the help and friendship I never got. I want to be the person I always needed in my life. I want to share with the children I teach the books that got me through my childhood and continue to get me through my young adult life. <br /><br />This book is one of those that I remember from my childhood as one of the most touching books I ever read. I consumed books when I was a child. I was always reading, I was never not reading. I had literal tubs of books that I would pull out and read from for a whole day. I adored my books; my books were my life, my escape from the world I grew up in. <br /><br />Out of those hundreds of books I read, I remember this one with a handful of others very well. Rereading Green Angel has only deepened my love for Green/Ash. I understand her. She understands me. We have both gone through desperate loss and we responded the same way. By the end of the novel, she begins to find a new beginning and that gives me hope that one day I will too.<br /><br />Hoffman’s writing is beautiful and perfect for this fairy tale-esque book. The book is small in form but packs a very large punch especially to the little girl, and now young woman, who can so easily understand pain, sorrow and rage. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15260184699996542364">This gorgeous little book (116 pages) was recommended to me by one of my tumblr friends, 3partsfool after we quizzed each other one night over what characters or books really touched us years later after reading the last page. <br/><br/>I could not thank her enough for sharing this book with me. Alice Hoffman is a wonderful author that has crossed many genres and age levels. Her stories are always well written and thought provoking, which is all I want when I read a piece of work. <br/><br/>This little novel is no </span>
  <span id="freeText15260184699996542364" style="display:none">This gorgeous little book (116 pages) was recommended to me by one of my tumblr friends, 3partsfool after we quizzed each other one night over what characters or books really touched us years later after reading the last page. <br /><br />I could not thank her enough for sharing this book with me. Alice Hoffman is a wonderful author that has crossed many genres and age levels. Her stories are always well written and thought provoking, which is all I want when I read a piece of work. <br /><br />This little novel is no exception. This story has a character that is unique in her own way but as well realistic and relatable. After facing the most devastating moment in her life, you watch Green (the main character) go from almost losing herself, to working her way back out in the world and trying to bring life back into her now hallow life. This novelette will really pull at your heart strings. When all seems lost, light and love always find their way even if it means you need to let go of certain loved ones in that journey. I will not say anything more about this novel for fear of revealing too much especially if you would like to read this on your own. <br /><br />I will promise that this character will stay with you long after you have read the last page and have placed this book back on the shelf.</span>

    <a title="AlexM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2559756-alexm"><img alt="AlexM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364263596p2/2559756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65128870?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AlexM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AlexM" href="/user/show/2559756-alexm">AlexM</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65128870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6543548391796996765">I really liked this story because it gives a deep perspective on Green's thoughts and feelings on everything that happens to her throught the story. Her parents and sister are killed in a fire at their house and Green goes through a transformation throught the story from the lighthearted Green to the sorrow-filled Ash. She goes through it because she loses herself by destroying her feeling but also destroying herself, inking ravens, bats, and roses into her skin. It is a very,very, good story. I</span>
  <span id="freeText6543548391796996765" style="display:none">I really liked this story because it gives a deep perspective on Green's thoughts and feelings on everything that happens to her throught the story. Her parents and sister are killed in a fire at their house and Green goes through a transformation throught the story from the lighthearted Green to the sorrow-filled Ash. She goes through it because she loses herself by destroying her feeling but also destroying herself, inking ravens, bats, and roses into her skin. It is a very,very, good story. I cannot put it into a genre because it is not a fantasy book, not a spiritual book, and not really a non-fiction book. I have to say that the relationship of a non-fiction book and a fiction book blurs into one. It is non-fiction book but has the elements of a fictional story but sometimes blurs into a little bit of a fantasy story. As for spiritual part of it is is not having faith in a god but having faith in yourself and never turning away to a darker side of your soul. It was a beautiful story to read and I hope that you like it to if you decide to read it. Alice Hoffman seems like a genius to me for writing Green Angel.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_224611395" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224611395" />
    <a title="Melanti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3034846-melanti"><img alt="Melanti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286146966p2/3034846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224611395?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanti" href="/user/show/3034846-melanti">Melanti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3034846-melanti?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224611395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8851124704571157929">Other than Hoffman's children's picture book, this is perhaps the most simplistic book of hers I've read yet. But while it's simple in plot, its rich in content. It's the story of shy, introverted Green who is the only person of her family to survive a horrible disaster and has to cope survivor's guilt and the changed town, including teenage looters.<br/><br/>I don't often judge a book by it's cover but I adore the cover on the hardback version; it seems to sum up the novel perfectly. The front is Green a</span>
  <span id="freeText8851124704571157929" style="display:none">Other than Hoffman's children's picture book, this is perhaps the most simplistic book of hers I've read yet. But while it's simple in plot, its rich in content. It's the story of shy, introverted Green who is the only person of her family to survive a horrible disaster and has to cope survivor's guilt and the changed town, including teenage looters.<br /><br />I don't often judge a book by it's cover but I adore the cover on the hardback version; it seems to sum up the novel perfectly. The front is Green as she was before the disaster: both decorated by and restrained by her garden, but not seeming to notice her fetters. The back, Garden as post-disaster Ash, facing away. Perhaps freer, with no restraining vines, a more assertive posture, but infinitely sadder and darker. Under the dust jacket - an empty plain full of nothing but loneliness and ravens.<br /><br />The story won't hold any surprises or twists to anyone familiar with Hoffman's other novels - she is rather formulaic (One of these days I'm going to find a book by Hoffman that has a truly happy ending, and I'll be stunned.) - but it's well worth the read if you enjoy fairy tale imagery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8851124704571157929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127585754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127585754" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4383168-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520024353p2/4383168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127585754?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/4383168-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4383168-amy?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127585754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1877925495351848803">I was bought this book for Christmas 2009, by my boyfriend's mother, who I love talking about books with. I asked her to choose me something I'd like and she chose well for me - I did like it. <br/><br/>Green Angel is a sweet and charming read about grief and how one young girl deals with it after losing her family in a fire. <br/><br/>Is it supposed to be aimed at younger readers? I've read several of Alice Hoffman's other books and they feel very different, in tone if not entirely in plot - although the post-apoc</span>
  <span id="freeText1877925495351848803" style="display:none">I was bought this book for Christmas 2009, by my boyfriend's mother, who I love talking about books with. I asked her to choose me something I'd like and she chose well for me - I did like it. <br /><br />Green Angel is a sweet and charming read about grief and how one young girl deals with it after losing her family in a fire. <br /><br />Is it supposed to be aimed at younger readers? I've read several of Alice Hoffman's other books and they feel very different, in tone if not entirely in plot - although the post-apocalyptic setting differs greatly from her usual small-town America, as in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/165818.The_River_King" title="The River King by Alice Hoffman" rel="nofollow noopener">The River King</a> and elsewhere. However, this use of non-location is the one thing that makes the book feel more powerful - in a sense, it could be anywhere. <br /><br />It was very poetic but in a way that I occasionally found try-hard and slightly irritating. This would have been one of my very favourite books if I'd read this at 14 or 15. As it is, I enjoyed it and found it entertaining and not at all depressing as many of the other reviewers have said here. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1877925495351848803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_489736079" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489736079" />
    <a title="Patricia J. O&#39;Brien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3946202-patricia-j-o-brien"><img alt="Patricia J. O&#39;Brien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294422452p2/3946202.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489736079?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia J. O&#39;Brien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia J. O&#39;Brien" href="/user/show/3946202-patricia-j-o-brien">Patricia J. O&#39;Brien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489736079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18249174910939792812">I read GREEN ANGEL years ago and wanted to revisit it, to see if I still thought it was a little gem. I do. It's a fairy tale, an allegory, told swiftly but with its soul intact.<br/>15-year-old Green gets her name from her skill with plants, on helping things to thrive and grow. Her family lives a rural life near a city where they sell their produce, but one day Green is left to tend the garden while her mother, father and sister go to market. On that day, terrorists attack and destroy the city, cau</span>
  <span id="freeText18249174910939792812" style="display:none">I read GREEN ANGEL years ago and wanted to revisit it, to see if I still thought it was a little gem. I do. It's a fairy tale, an allegory, told swiftly but with its soul intact.<br />15-year-old Green gets her name from her skill with plants, on helping things to thrive and grow. Her family lives a rural life near a city where they sell their produce, but one day Green is left to tend the garden while her mother, father and sister go to market. On that day, terrorists attack and destroy the city, causing an apocalyptic cloud of ash and embers that spreads across the river to the farm where Green is watching in horror until she is almost completely blind.<br />Green's loss and pain and hopelessness lead her to change her name to Ash, to ink thorny vines on her skin and give up on the future. I don't want to give any more away, except to say this is a story of rebirth and renewal, told in heartbreakingly beautiful imagery.<br />And as seems to be the way with Alice Hoffman, magic weaves its way into ordinary life in fascinating ways.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18249174910939792812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0RKmjdKLW+6NYz+NWnd5BTBUDXC30nIi7rIf1kkeJPJIA1po7/sdAPwNcoZbh8JtaZUTNs2rSjsEJOIyhUTTlw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EFkvSaKS//CB8p7XnnLfcVk34xfwGdH7zHaAg2cZFBuJSNOsn+K5HvCc09yfgmQZAPb9UYpg6eIm4H1nq0Pjfg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3417564693376668520">Alice Hoffman is the author of more than thirty works of fiction, including The World That We Knew, The Rules of Magic, The Marriage of Opposites, Practical Magic, The Red Garden, the Oprah’s Book Club selection Here on Earth, The Museum of Extraordinary Things, and The Dovekeepers. Her most recent novel is The World That We Knew. She lives near Boston.</span>
